						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pothohari_language&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Pothohari language">Pothohari language</a>)</span></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Indo-Aryan language variety spoken in Pakistan</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above above" style="font-size:125%; color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;">Pahari-Pothwari</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader" style="font-size:110%; color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">پوٹھواری</span>, <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">پہاڑی</span> <br /> Poṭhwārī, Pahāṛī</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Pahari-Pothwari.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Pahari-Pothwari.png/200px-Pahari-Pothwari.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="181" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Pahari-Pothwari.png/300px-Pahari-Pothwari.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Pahari-Pothwari.png/400px-Pahari-Pothwari.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="475" /></a></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Native&#160;to</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Region</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Pothohar_Plateau" title="Pothohar Plateau">Pothohar</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_Punjab" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani Punjab">Punjab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azad_Kashmir" title="Azad Kashmir">Azad Kashmir</a> and western parts of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)">Jammu and Kashmir</a>, other parts of India including <a href="/wiki/Punjab_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjab (India)">Punjab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a> (by partition refugees and descendants)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Native speakers</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">several million<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">Language family</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><div style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a>
<ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>
<a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranian_languages" title="Indo-Iranian languages">Indo-Iranian</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Indo-Aryan_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwestern Indo-Aryan languages">Northwestern</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Punjabic_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjabic languages">Punjabi</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Lahnda" title="Lahnda">Lahnda (Western Punjabi)</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><b>Pahari-Pothwari</b></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">Writing system</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Shahmukhi" title="Shahmukhi">Shahmukhi</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">ISO 639-3</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a href="https://iso639-3.sil.org/code/phr" class="extiw" title="iso639-3:phr">phr</a></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><i><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></i></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://glottolog.org/resource/languoid/id/paha1251">paha1251</a></code>&#160; Pahari Potwari</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Pahari-Pothwari</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a> <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">language variety</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lahnda" title="Lahnda">Lahnda</a> group,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> spoken on the <a href="/wiki/Pothohar_Plateau" title="Pothohar Plateau">Pothohar Plateau</a> in the far north of <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab, Pakistan</a>, as well as in most of Pakistan-administered <a href="/wiki/Azad_Kashmir" title="Azad Kashmir">Azad Kashmir</a> and in western areas of Indian-administered <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)">Jammu and Kashmir</a>, is known by a variety of names, the most common of which are <b>Pahari</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small>English: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pahari_language" title="Pahari language">an ambiguous name</a> also applied to other unrelated languages of India), and <b>Pothwari</b> (or <b>Pothohari</b>).
</p><p>The language is transitional between <a href="/wiki/Hindko_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindko language">Hindko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Punjabi" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Punjabi">Standard Punjabi</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShackle1979200–201_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShackle1979200–201-4">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and is mutually intelligible with both.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> There have been efforts at cultivation as a literary language,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasica1991440_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasica1991440-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> although a local standard has not been established yet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShackle1983183_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShackle1983183-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shahmukhi" title="Shahmukhi">Shahmukhi</a> script is used to write the language, such as in the works of <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> poet <a href="/wiki/Mian_Muhammad_Bakhsh" title="Mian Muhammad Bakhsh">Mian Muhammad Bakhsh</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/George_Abraham_Grierson" title="George Abraham Grierson">Grierson</a> in his early 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_Survey_of_India" title="Linguistic Survey of India">Linguistic Survey of India</a> assigned it to a so-called "Northern cluster" of <a href="/wiki/Lahnda" title="Lahnda">Lahnda</a> (Western Punjabi), but this classification, as well as the validity of the Lahnda grouping in this case, have been called into question.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShackle1979201_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShackle1979201-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In a sense both Pothwari, as well as other Lahnda varieties, and Standard Punjabi are "dialects" of a "<a href="/wiki/Punjabi_dialects_and_languages" title="Punjabi dialects and languages">Greater Punjabi"</a> macrolanguage.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to effects of dominant languages in Pakistani media like Urdu, Standard Punjabi and English and religious impact of Arabic and Persian, Pahari-Pothwari like other regional varieties of Pakistan are continuously expanding its vocabulary base with loan words.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution_and_dialects">Geographic distribution and dialects</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px">
<div class="thumbcaption">
<a class="mw-kartographer-map mw-kartographer-container center" style="width: 300px; height: 300px;" data-mw-kartographer="mapframe" data-style="osm-intl" data-width="300" data-height="300" data-zoom="7" data-lat="33.8" data-lon="73.7" data-overlays="[&quot;_147148caa955248ab3c4a208822d0e0db6e95225&quot;]" href="/wiki/Special:Map/7/33.8/73.7/en"><img src="https://maps.wikimedia.org/img/osm-intl,7,33.8,73.7,300x300.png?lang=en&amp;domain=en.wikipedia.org&amp;title=Pahari-Pothwari&amp;revid=1208701976&amp;groups=_147148caa955248ab3c4a208822d0e0db6e95225" width="300" height="300" decoding="async" srcset="https://maps.wikimedia.org/img/osm-intl,7,33.8,73.7,300x300@2x.png?lang=en&amp;domain=en.wikipedia.org&amp;title=Pahari-Pothwari&amp;revid=1208701976&amp;groups=_147148caa955248ab3c4a208822d0e0db6e95225 2x" alt="Map" /></a> </div>
<div class="thumbcaption"><a class="mw-kartographer-maplink" data-mw-kartographer="maplink" data-style="osm-intl" href="/wiki/Special:Map/7/33.8/73.7/en" data-zoom="7" data-lat="33.8" data-lon="73.7" data-overlays="[&quot;_a6d5e6a286f15cb13f216cfa3509f64d93b9903c&quot;]"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1038841319">.mw-parser-output .tooltip-dotted{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}</style><span class="rt-commentedText tooltip tooltip-dotted" title="Click for interactive fullscreen map with links to nearby articles">[fullscreen map]</span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">Azad Kashmir and surrounding areas with some of the locations mentioned in this section. Places where Pahari–Pothwari is spoken are in <span style="color:darkred">dark red</span>.</div>
</div></div>
<p>There are at least three major dialects: Pothwari, Mirpuri and Pahari.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> The Pothwari spoken in <a href="/wiki/Gujar_Khan" title="Gujar Khan">Gujar Khan</a> is regarded as the most prestigious dialect of Pothwari spoken in Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The dialects are mutually intelligible,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> but the difference between the northernmost and the southernmost dialects (from <a href="/wiki/Muzaffarabad_District" title="Muzaffarabad District">Muzaffarabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirpur_District" title="Mirpur District">Mirpur</a> respectively) is enough to cause difficulties in understanding.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201086_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201086-14">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pothohar_Plateau">Pothohar Plateau</span></h3>
<p>Pothwari (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;"><span title="Potwari-language text"><span lang="phr" dir="rtl">پوٹھواری</span></span></span>), also spelt <i>Potwari</i>, <i>Potohari</i> and <i>Pothohari</i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;"><span title="Potwari-language text"><span lang="phr" dir="rtl">پوٹھوہاری</span></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> is spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Pothohar_Plateau" title="Pothohar Plateau">Pothohar Plateau</a> of northern <a href="/wiki/Punjab" title="Punjab">Punjab</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbasiAsif2010201_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbasiAsif2010201-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> an area administratively within <a href="/wiki/Rawalpindi_Division" title="Rawalpindi Division">Rawalpindi division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919432_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919432-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Pothwari is its most common name, and some call it <i><a href="/wiki/Rawalpindi_District" title="Rawalpindi District">Pindiwal</a> <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a></i> to differentiate it from the Punjabi spoken elsewhere in Punjab.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Tilla_Jogian.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tilla_Jogian.jpg/250px-Tilla_Jogian.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tilla_Jogian.jpg/375px-Tilla_Jogian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tilla_Jogian.jpg/500px-Tilla_Jogian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Pothwar scenery with hill backdrop</figcaption></figure>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:North_Lahnda_Map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/North_Lahnda_Map.png/246px-North_Lahnda_Map.png" decoding="async" width="246" height="246" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/North_Lahnda_Map.png/369px-North_Lahnda_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/North_Lahnda_Map.png/492px-North_Lahnda_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1080" /></a><figcaption>Geographic distribution of various Pahari languages and dialects across the Lower Himalayas. (Blue - Pahari-Pothwari, Purple - Hindko)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Pothwari extends southwards up to the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Range" title="Salt Range">Salt Range</a>, with the city of <a href="/wiki/Jhelum" title="Jhelum">Jhelum</a> marking the border with Majha Punjabi. To the north, Pothwari transitions into the Pahari-speaking area, with <a href="/wiki/Bhara_Kahu" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhara Kahu">Bharakao</a>, near Islamabad, generally regarded as the point where Pothwari ends and Pahari begins.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102–3,_19,_112_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102–3,_19,_112-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Pothwari has been represented by their own people and their own community as they re-presented with their own ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShackle1983183_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShackle1983183-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>, 85.1% of households had Pothwari as mother tongue.
</p><p>Among the dialects of the Pahari-Pothwari dialect cluster, the variety spoken on the Pothohar is the only native language in the Rawalpindi division and it is ethno-linguistic group.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This Pothwari is also regarded as the most prestigious dialect spoken in the region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mirpur">Mirpur</span></h3>
<p>East of the Pothwari areas, across the <a href="/wiki/Jhelum_River" title="Jhelum River">Jhelum River</a> into <a href="/wiki/Mirpur_District" title="Mirpur District">Mirpur District</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azad_Kashmir" title="Azad Kashmir">Azad Kashmir</a>, the language is more similar to Pothwari than to the Pahari spoken in the rest of Azad Kashmir.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201212,_26._At_least_in_terms_of_lexical_similarity._21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201212,_26._At_least_in_terms_of_lexical_similarity.-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
Locally it is known by a variety of names:<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> <i>Pahari</i>, <i>Mirpur Pahari</i>, <i>Mirpuri</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Pothwari</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102–3,_5,_19,_100_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102–3,_5,_19,_100-24">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> while some of its speakers call it <i>Punjabi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201044_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201044-25">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
Mirpuris possess a strong sense of Kashmiri identity that overrides linguistic identification with closely related groups outside Azad Kashmir, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pothohar_Plateau" title="Pothohar Plateau">Pothwari</a> <a href="/wiki/Punjabis" title="Punjabis">Punjabis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShackle2007114_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShackle2007114-26">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
The Mirpur region has been the source of the greater part of Pakistani immigration to the UK, a process that started when thousands were displaced by the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Mangla_Dam" title="Mangla Dam">Mangla Dam</a> in the 1960s and emigrated to fill labour shortages in England.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20121_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20121-27">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/British_Mirpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mirpuri">British Mirpuri</a> diaspora now numbers several hundred thousand, and Pahari has been argued to be the second most common mother tongue in the UK, yet the language is little known in the wider society there and its status has remained surrounded by confusion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHussain2015483–84_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHussain2015483–84-28">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Kashmir.2C_Murree_and_the_Galyat"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kashmir,_Murree_and_the_Galyat">Kashmir, Murree and the Galyat</span></h3>
<p>Pahari (<span title="Potwari-language text"><span lang="phr"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">پہاڑی</span></span></span>) is spoken to the north of Pothwari. The central cluster of Pahari dialects is found around <a href="/wiki/Murree" title="Murree">Murree</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201023_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201023-29">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> This area is in the <a href="/wiki/Galyat" title="Galyat">Galyat</a>: the hill country of <a href="/wiki/Murree_Tehsil" title="Murree Tehsil">Murree Tehsil</a> in the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Rawalpindi_District" title="Rawalpindi District">Rawalpindi District</a> (just north of the capital Islamabad) and the adjoining areas in southeastern <a href="/wiki/Abbottabad_District" title="Abbottabad District">Abbottabad District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102,_5_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102,_5-30">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> One name occasionally found in the literature for this language is <i><b>Dhundi-Kairali</b></i> (<i>Ḍhūṇḍī-Kaiṛālī</i>), a term first used by <a href="/wiki/G.A._Grierson" class="mw-redirect" title="G.A. Grierson">Grierson</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbasi2010104_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbasi2010104-31">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> who based it on the names of the two major tribes of the area – the <a href="/wiki/Kairal_tribe" class="mw-redirect" title="Kairal tribe">Kairal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dhund_Abbasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhund Abbasi">Dhund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbasiAsif2010201_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbasiAsif2010201-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Its speakers call it <i>Pahari</i> in Murree tehsil, while in Abbottabad district it is known as either <i>Hindko</i> or <i>Ḍhūṇḍī</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
Nevertheless, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hindko" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Hindko">Hindko</a> – properly the language of the rest of Abbottabad District and the neighbouring areas of Khyber Pakhtunkhwa  – is generally regarded as a different language.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201040,_126–27_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201040,_126–27-33">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> It forms a <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a> with Pahari, <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbasiAsif2010201_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbasiAsif2010201-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and the transition between the two is in northern Azad Kashmir and in the Galyat region. For example, on the road from Murree northwest towards the city of Abbottabad, Pahari gradually changes into Hindko between <a href="/wiki/Ayubia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayubia">Ayubia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nathiagali" class="mw-redirect" title="Nathiagali">Nathiagali</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102,_40_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102,_40-34">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png/249px-Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png" decoding="async" width="249" height="249" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png/374px-Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png/498px-Pahari-Pothwari-Hindko_Dialects.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1080" /></a><figcaption>Distribution of Pahari-Pothwari dialects with subdivisions overlayed</figcaption></figure>
<p>A closely related dialect is spoken across the Jhelum River in Azad Kashmir, north of the Mirpuri areas. Names associated in the literature with this dialect are <i>Pahari</i> (itself the term most commonly used by the speakers themselves), <i><b>Chibhālī</b></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102,_5,_8_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers20102,_5,_8-35">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> named after the <a href="/wiki/Chibhal" title="Chibhal">Chibhal</a> region<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919505_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919505-36">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> or the Chibh ethnic group,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919432_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919432-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and <i><b>Poonchi</b></i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;"><span title="Potwari-language text"><span lang="phr" dir="rtl">پونچھی</span></span></span>, also spelt <i>Punchhi</i>). The latter name has been variously applied to either the Chibhali variety specific to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poonch_District" title="History of Poonch District">district of Poonch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919p._505_and_corresponding_map_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrierson1919p._505_and_corresponding_map-37">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> or to the dialect of the whole northern half of Azad Kashmir.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> 
This dialect (or dialects) has been seen either as a separate dialect from the one in Murree,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbasi2010104_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbasi2010104-31">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> or as belonging to the same central group of Pahari dialects.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers2010sec._3.1_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers2010sec._3.1-39">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The dialect of the <a href="/wiki/Bagh_District" title="Bagh District">district of Bagh</a>, for example, has more shared vocabulary with the core dialects from Murree (86–88%) than with the varieties of either Muzaffarabad (84%) or Mirpur (78%).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Muzaffarabad_District" title="Muzaffarabad District">Muzaffarabad</a> the dialect shows lexical similarity<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> of 83–88% with the central group of Pahari dialects, which is high enough for the authors of the sociolinguistic survey to classify it is a central dialect itself, but low enough to warrant noting its borderline status.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201024–25_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201024–25-42">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The speakers however tend to call their language <i>Hindko</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201026,_80_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201026,_80-43">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and to identify more with the Hindko spoken to the west,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers2010108,_110_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers2010108,_110-44">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> despite the lower lexical similarity (73–79%) with the core Hindko dialects of <a href="/wiki/Abbottabad" title="Abbottabad">Abbottabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mansehra" title="Mansehra">Mansehra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201024_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELothersLothers201024-45">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Further north into the <a href="/wiki/Neelam_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Neelam Valley">Neelam Valley</a> the dialect, now known locally as <i>Parmi</i>, becomes closer to Hindko.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pahari is also spoken further east across the <a href="/wiki/Line_of_Control" title="Line of Control">Line of Control</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Pir_Panjal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pir Panjal">Pir Panjal</a> mountains in Indian <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)">Jammu and Kashmir</a>. The population, estimated at 1 million,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> is found in the region between the <a href="/wiki/Jhelum_River" title="Jhelum River">Jhelum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chenab" class="mw-redirect" title="Chenab">Chenab</a> rivers: most significantly in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Poonch_district,_India" title="Poonch district, India">Poonch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rajouri_district" title="Rajouri district">Rajouri</a>, to a lesser extent in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Baramulla_district" title="Baramulla district">Baramulla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kupwara_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Kupwara District">Kupwara</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and also – as a result of the influx of refugees during the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition</a> of 1947 – scattered throughout the rest of Jammu and Kashmir.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Pahari is among the regional languages listed in the sixth schedule of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Constitution of Jammu and Kashmir">Constitution of Jammu and Kashmir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> This Pahari is sometimes conflated with the <a href="/wiki/Western_Pahari" title="Western Pahari">Western Pahari</a> languages spoken in the mountainous region in the south-east of Indian Jammu and Kashmir. These languages, which include <a href="/wiki/Bhadarwahi" title="Bhadarwahi">Bhadarwahi</a> and its neighbours, are often called "Pahari", although not same they are closely related to Pahari–Pothwari.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaul200642,_256–8_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaul200642,_256–8-51">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>A long diphthong /ɑi/ can be realized as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[äː]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li>Sounds <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[f,<span class="wrap"> </span>ʒ,<span class="wrap"> </span>χ,<span class="wrap"> </span>ʁ,<span class="wrap"> </span>q]</span> are heard from Persian and Arabic loanwords.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> is realized as voiced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɦ]</span> in word-initial position.</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> before a velar consonant can be heard as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ŋ]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Features">Notable Features</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_Tense">Future Tense</span></h3>
<p>The future tense in Pothwari is formed by adding -s as opposed to the Eastern Punjabi <i>gā.</i><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This tense is also used in other <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_varieties" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjabi varieties">Western Punjabi dialects</a> such as the Jatki dialects, <a href="/wiki/Shahpuri_dialect" title="Shahpuri dialect">Shahpuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jhangochi" class="mw-redirect" title="Jhangochi">Jhangochi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhanni_dialect" title="Dhanni dialect">Dhanni</a>, as well as in and <a href="/wiki/Hindko" title="Hindko">Hindko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saraiki_language" title="Saraiki language">Saraiki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th rowspan="2"><b>English</b>
</th>
<th colspan="3"><b>Pothwari</b>
</th>
<th colspan="3"><b>Eastern Punjabi</b>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th><b>Transliteration</b>

</th>
<th><b><a href="/wiki/Gurmukhi" title="Gurmukhi">Gurmukhi</a></b>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>I will do
</td>
<td>Mãi karsā̃
</td>
<td><span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">مَیں کرساں</span></span>
</td>
<td>ਮੈਂ ਕਰਸਾਂ
</td>
<td>Mãi karāngā
</td>
<td><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">مَیں کرانگا</span>
</td>
<td>ਮੈਂ ਕਰਾਂਗਾ
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>We will do
</td>
<td>Asā̃ karsā̃

<td>ਓਹ ਕਰਣਗੇ
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This type of future tense was also used by classical Punjabi poets. Punjabi poet <a href="/wiki/Bulleh_Shah" title="Bulleh Shah">Bulleh Shah</a> sometimes uses a similar form of future tense in his poetry<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Shahmukhi: جو کُجھ کَرسین, سو کُجھ پاسیں</i>
</p><p><i>Transliteration: Jo kujh karsãi, so kujh paasãi</i>
</p><p><i>Translation: Whatsoever you do, is what you shall gain</i>
</p><p>- From one of Bulleh Shah's poems<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuous_Tense">Continuous Tense</span></h3>
<p>Similar to <a href="/wiki/Shahpuri_dialect" title="Shahpuri dialect">Jatki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindko" title="Hindko">Hindko</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_varieties" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjabi varieties">Western Punjabi dialects</a>, Pothwari also uses <i>pyā</i> to signify the continuous tense.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-58">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some <a href="/wiki/Majhi_dialect" title="Majhi dialect">Majhi</a> sub-dialects also utilize this tense.
</p>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The place of "<i>pyā"</i> may sometimes be switched with respect to the verb.
</p><p><i>"Tusā̃ bahoon changā kamm paye karnay o"</i>, meaning "You (plural) are doing a very good thing"
</p><p><i>"Mãi vi tān ehe gall karnā sān pyā"</i>, meaning "I was also saying the same thing"
</p><p><i>"Mãi vi tān ehe gall pyā karna aan"</i>, meaning "I am also saying the same thing"
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_Tense">Past Tense</span></h3>
<p>The past tense in Pothwari resembles that of Eastern Punjabi, however depending on the dialect, there may be slight variations.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tribal_groupings">Tribal groupings</span></h3>
<p>Pahari-Pothwari speakers belong to the same tribes found in Punjab. While the names of the tribes remain the same, the Punjabi word for tribe <i>Birādrī/Barādarī</i> (<span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">برادری</span></span>) becomes <i>Bilādrī/Balādarī</i> (<span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">بل ادری</span></span>) in Pahari-Pothwari.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbering_system">Numbering system</span></h3>
<p>Pahari-Pothwari follows the numbering traditions of Standard Punjabi. A point of departure from Eastern Punjabi dialects occurs in the use of <i><b>Trai</b></i> (<span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">ترَے</span></span>) instead of <i>Tinn</i> (<span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">تِنّ</span></span>) for the number 3. <a href="/wiki/Lahnda" title="Lahnda">Western Punjabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doabi" class="mw-redirect" title="Doabi">Doabi</a> also tend to use <i>trai</i> over <i>tinn</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly, Pothwari and other Western Punjabi dialects use <b><i>"Yārā̃"</i> (یاراں)</b> for <i>"Gyarā̃"</i> (گیاراں), <b><i>"Trei</i>" (ترئی)</b> for <i>"Tei"</i> (تئی) <b>"<i>Panji"</i> (پنجِی)</b> for <i>"Pachchi"</i> (پچّی) and <i>"<b>Trih"</b></i> <b>(ترِیہہ)</b> for <i>"Tih"</i> (تِیہہ), for the numbers 11, 23, 25, and 30.
</p>

<p><b>Ordinals</b>
</p><p>The ordinal numbers are largely the same. The only difference occurs in the words for <i>Second</i> and <i>Third</i>. Second is <i>Doowa</i> (دووا) in Pothwari, whilst it is <i>Dooja</i> (دوجا) in Punjabi. Likewise Third is <i>Treeya</i> (تریا) in Pothwari whilst it is <i>Teeja</i> (تیجا) in Punjabi. <a href="/wiki/Lahnda" title="Lahnda">Western Punjabi</a> in general tends to follow this trend.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possessive_pronouns">Possessive pronouns</span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Object_marker">Object marker</span></h3>
<p>The object marker in Pothwari is <i>kī</i> (ਕੀ /کی) as opposed to <i>nū̃</i> (ਨੂੰ / نوں) in Standard Punjabi.
</p><p>For example:
</p><p>The phrase: <i>lokkā̃ <b>nū̃</b></i> (ਲੋਕਾਂ <b>ਨੂੰ</b> / لوکاں <b>نوں</b>), meaning "to the people" in Standard Punjabi, would become <i>lokkā̃ <b>kī</b></i> (ਲੋਕਾਂ <b>ਕੀ</b> / لوکاں <b>کی</b>) in Pothwari.
</p><p>Hence, the personal pronouns would be as follows:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genitive_marker">Genitive marker</span></h3>
<p>The genitive marker in Pothwari is represented through the use of <i>nā</i> (ਨਾ / <span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">نا</span></span>) as opposed to <i>dā</i> (ਦਾ / <span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">دا</span></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For example:
</p><p>The phrase: <i>lokkā̃ <b>dā</b></i> (ਲੋਕਾਂ <b>ਦਾ</b> / <span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">لوکاں <strong>دا</strong></span></span>), meaning "people's" or "of the people" in Pothwari, would become <i>lokkā̃ <b>nā</b></i> (ਲੋਕਾਂ <b>ਨਾ</b> / <span style="font-size:90%;"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">لوکاں <strong>نا</strong></span></span>).
</p><p>This also affects some of the possessive pronouns as described above.
</p><p>It should also be noted that in Pothwari, the present form of verb does not end with the standard <i>dā</i> sound either, and is replaced with <i>nā.</i>
</p><p>For example:
</p><p><i>Miki eh nahi si <b>chāhinā</b></i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">میکی ایہہ نہیں سی چاہی نا</span>), meaning "This is not what I wanted"
</p><p><i>Oh kay pyā <b>ākhnā</b> ae?</i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">اوہ کے پیا آخنا اے؟</span>), meaning "What is he saying?"
</p><p>This also affects the common Punjabi passive tense:
</p><p><i>Isrā̃ nahi <b>ākhee nā</b></i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">اِسراں نہیں آکھی نا</span>), instead of "<i><b>ākhee dā</b></i>", meaning "This is now how it should be said"
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oblique_case_of_nouns">Oblique case of nouns</span></h3>
<p>Pothwari has unique forms for nouns in oblique cases. This is not observed in Standard Punjabi, but is seen in <a href="/wiki/Hindko" title="Hindko">Hindko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Words_for_.22Coming.22_and_.22Going.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Words_for_&quot;Coming&quot;_and_&quot;Going&quot;">Words for "Coming" and "Going"</span></h3>
<p>The Pothwari word for "coming" is <i><b>acchṇā</b></i>, whereas for "going" <i><b>gacchṇā</b>, <b>julṇā</b></i> and <i><b>jāṇā</b></i> are used.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-62">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The imperative for <i><b>gacchṇā</b></i> is both <i>gacch</i> and <i>gau</i>.
</p>

<h3><span id="Words_used_for_.22Taking.22_and_.22Bringing.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Words_used_for_&quot;Taking&quot;_and_&quot;Bringing&quot;">Words used for "Taking" and "Bringing"</span></h3>
<p>Commonly observed in the <a href="/wiki/Lahnda_dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="Lahnda dialects">Lahnda dialects</a> is the use of <i>Ghinṇā</i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">گھِننا</span>)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Aaṇnā</i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">آننا</span>)<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> instead of the Eastern Punjabi words <i>Laiṇā</i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">لَینا</span>) and <i>Lyāṇā</i> (<span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS_Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">لیانا</span>).
</p><p>Notice how <i>Ghin āo</i> becomes <i><b>Ghini achho</b></i>, and <i>Ghin ghidā</i> becomes <i><b>Ghini ghidā</b></i> in accordance with Pothwari grammar and vocabulary.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irregular_past_tense_of_verbs">Irregular past tense of verbs</span></h3>
<p>Pothwari generally follows the common Punjabi irregular verbs (e.g. <i>khādhā, peetā, nahātā, dhotā, moyā, latthā, khalotā, ḍaṭṭhā, suttā, keetā, dittā, ghidā, seetā, baddhā</i>).
</p><p>Some additional forms are observed in <i><b>bantā</b></i> (بنتا) for <i>banyā</i> and <i><b>khaltā</b></i> (کھلتا) for <i>khalā.</i>
</p><p>For example:
</p><p><i>Miki sarkay apar <b>khaltyon</b> addhā ghantā hoi gya sā</i>
</p><p><i>Menu sark tey khalyā̃/khlotyā̃ addhā ghantā ho gya si</i>
</p><p>(It had been an hour since I was waiting on the road)
</p><p><i>Chā kadon ni <b>banti</b> hoi ae</i>
</p><p><i>Chā kadon di bani hoi ae</i>
</p><p>(The tea has been ready for quite some time)
</p>

<td>Why
</td>

<p>ਕੀਆਂ

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBaart2003">Baart (2003</a>, p.&#160;10) provides an estimate of 3.8 million, presumably for the population in Pakistan alone. <a href="#CITEREFLothersLothers2010">Lothers &amp; Lothers (2010</a>, p.&#160;9) estimate the Pakistani population at well over 2.5 million and the UK diaspora at over 0.5 million. The population in India is reported in <a href="#CITEREFEthnologue2017">Ethnologue (2017)</a> to be about 1 million as of 2000.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There is no consensus among linguists or Pahari-Pothwari speakers in terms of its status as a dialect of Punjabi or a separate language entirely. For the difficulties in assigning the labels "language" and "dialect", see <a href="#CITEREFShackle1979">Shackle (1979)</a> for Punjabi and <a href="#CITEREFMasica1991">Masica (1991</a>, pp.&#160;23–27) for <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a> generally.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to <a href="#CITEREFLothersLothers2010">Lothers &amp; Lothers (2010</a>, p.&#160;2). <a href="#CITEREFAbbasi2010">Abbasi (2010</a>, p.&#160;104) adds as a fourth dialect the <i>Poonchi</i> spoken from Poonch to the Neelam Valley. Yet another classification is reportedly presented in <a href="#CITEREFKarnai2007">Karnai (2007)</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> For example, according to <a href="#CITEREF1981_Census_report_Rawalpindi">the 1981 census report for Rawalpindi District</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One language activist from the diaspora in Britain "[has] said that he does not give the language a single name because those who speak the language call it many different things." (<a href="#CITEREFLothersLothers2012">Lothers &amp; Lothers 2012</a>, p.&#160;3). </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some, at least in the British diaspora, consider this term to be a misnomer if applied to the language. (<a href="#CITEREFLothersLothers2012">Lothers &amp; Lothers 2012</a>, p.&#160;3). </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The similarity between wordlists containing 217 items of basic vocabulary from each location. (<a href="#CITEREFLothersLothers2010">Lothers &amp; Lothers 2010</a>, pp.&#160;15–16) </span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFLothersLothers2010">Lothers &amp; Lothers 2010</a>, p.&#160;26; <a href="#CITEREFAkhtarRehman2007">Akhtar &amp; Rehman 2007</a>, p.&#160;68. The conclusion is similarly based on lexical similarity and the comparison is with the Hindko of the <a href="/wiki/Kaghan_Valley" title="Kaghan Valley">Kaghan Valley</a> on one hand and with the Pahari of the Murre Hills on the other.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A 2000 estimate reported in <a href="#CITEREFEthnologue2017">Ethnologue (2017)</a></span>
</li>

</li>
